    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer7804870196785043617">Cas Lowood has inherited an unusual vocation: He kills the dead.<br/><br/>So did his father before him, until he was gruesomely murdered by a ghost he sought to kill. Now, armed with his father's mysterious and deadly athame, Cas travels the country with his kitchen-witch mother and their spirit-sniffing cat. They follow legends and local lore, destroy the murderous dead, and keep p</span>
  <span id="freeText7804870196785043617" style="display:none">Cas Lowood has inherited an unusual vocation: He kills the dead.<br /><br />So did his father before him, until he was gruesomely murdered by a ghost he sought to kill. Now, armed with his father's mysterious and deadly athame, Cas travels the country with his kitchen-witch mother and their spirit-sniffing cat. They follow legends and local lore, destroy the murderous dead, and keep pesky things like the future and friends at bay.<br /><br />Searching for a ghost the locals call Anna Dressed in Blood, Cas expects the usual: track, hunt, kill. What he finds instead is a girl entangled in curses and rage, a ghost like he's never faced before. She still wears the dress she wore on the day of her brutal murder in 1958: once white, now stained red and dripping with blood. Since her death, Anna has killed any and every person who has dared to step into the deserted Victorian she used to call home.<br /><br />Yet she spares Cas's life.</span>

<div id="review_236244760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236244760" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236244760?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=death-is-not-the-end">death-is-not-the-end</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236244760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17192459502720907354"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363272i/714526._SX540_.jpg' width='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>a million stars for anna dressed in awesome.<br/><br/>i was so hoping to be scared by this book. the way i was hoping to cry reading <i>a monster calls</i>. and it is fine that i wasn't and that i didn't - apparently i have no discernible human emotional response except an ability to become enthusiastic over well-written prose. and that's enough, for a life.<br/><br/>i don't even care that this book wasn't scary - it was so fun, and that is usually all i need to be riveted. did it have flaws? sure! were there things in th</span>
  <span id="freeText17192459502720907354" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363272i/714526._SX540_.jpg" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>a million stars for anna dressed in awesome.<br><br>i was so hoping to be scared by this book. the way i was hoping to cry reading <i>a monster calls</i>. and it is fine that i wasn't and that i didn't - apparently i have no discernible human emotional response except an ability to become enthusiastic over well-written prose. and that's enough, for a life.<br><br>i don't even care that this book wasn't scary - it was so fun, and that is usually all i need to be riveted. did it have flaws? sure! were there things in the book that occurred that made me pause? naturally. but overall, i found her voice so refreshing and her characters so likable, that none of it matters. this is a well-told story. <br><br>i thought this was more beautiful than scary. really, karen? even with all the ripped-up corpses and blood everywhere?? yup! i really did. i read it as a ghost who had a shitty life, and couldn't even get any peace after she was dead, and a boy who was missing out on his childhood because of an overdeveloped sense of justice and revenge. and of first love and first friendship and faith. secular faith. and there were so many genuinely funny moments (i do love this kid), and one terrible thing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ nooo, not tybalt!! why?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. definitely a well-executed book, and there are more to come?? sign me up right now.<br><br>a note on cursing. i am no lady, i am pretty comfortable with a wide range of salty talk. and sometimes, you can tell that some teen fiction is just dropping its f-bombs to shock or titillate its audience, all commiserating "oooh - don't tell the grownups!!" this was a book in full control of its potty mouth. a rainbow of expletives, masterfully handled. it brought a tear to the eye to see such a well-developed sense of vulgarity. again, not for shock value, but just the way kids curse. only funnier. and more elegantly. it is an art, after all. most kids use it as a weapon.<br><br>so between that, the maroon type (sucker for that), and the pathos and humor, this was an easy five-star book. i may never be scared of a book again, but at least i can still be entertained.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17192459502720907354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_165644475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165644475" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/165644475?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Hold Me Closer, Necromancer</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Wendy Darling by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=deliciously-creepy">deliciously-creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gorgeous-prose">gorgeous-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=heroines-butt-kicking">heroines-butt-kicking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=favorite-ya">favorite-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-ghosts">pn-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-favorites">2011-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165644475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9521177492367043121">Have you ever stood in your house, listening to a quiet, unfamiliar noise, and felt the hair rise on the back of your neck? Cas Lowood has, and the unholy hell of what he finds when he investigates will make you jump a little bit in your seat. He's a 17-year-old who kills the dead with a magic athame, just as his father did before him--and now he's faced with the task of killing Anna, a homicidal ghost who was murdered more than 60 years ago.<br/><br/>Cas is a fantastically strong and appealing protagonis</span>
  <span id="freeText9521177492367043121" style="display:none">Have you ever stood in your house, listening to a quiet, unfamiliar noise, and felt the hair rise on the back of your neck? Cas Lowood has, and the unholy hell of what he finds when he investigates will make you jump a little bit in your seat. He's a 17-year-old who kills the dead with a magic athame, just as his father did before him--and now he's faced with the task of killing Anna, a homicidal ghost who was murdered more than 60 years ago.<br /><br />Cas is a fantastically strong and appealing protagonist, but it's really Anna who takes center stage. Imagine the visual of a pale girl with inky hair floating in a dark house, her beautiful white dress slowly drip-drip-dripping with blood. She's deadly dangerous and full of vengeful fury, however, because of the way she was killed. When you find out what really happened to Anna, it's hard not to feel terrible pity for her--and to understand why Cas has such a hard time killing her.<br /><br />If you've been looking for a great YA horror novel, look no further. <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> is a stunning novel, full of atmospheric spookiness and unthinkable horrors. I cringed reading about ghosts with stones where their eyes should be, I yelped when Cas goes down into a basement full of...dreadful things, and my eyes got as big as saucers when the walls starting bleeding. But although the descriptions are full of vivid imagery and there's plenty of brutal action, what happens isn't at all gross. If anything, there's a dark beauty in the descriptions and an elegance in the writing that makes every scene a true pleasure to read. My reading status updates will give you a peek at some of the lines and scenes that particularly made me shiver, but I really had to restrain myself from posting one every couple of pages, as there's so much to savor, even in simple but humorous lines such as "She's wearing the same smile as her cat." I found just as much to love in the writing as I did the fantastic story, and the cheeky humor made me laugh even in dire and inappropriate circumstances.<br /><br />This is the darker, more grown-up version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8041873.Hold_Me_Closer__Necromancer" title="Hold Me Closer, Necromancer by Lish McBride" rel="nofollow noopener">Hold Me Closer, Necromancer</a>, and it's much more violent and much more polished. <i>Anna</i> offers an unforgettable thrill of a ride--and it catapulted instantly to my favorites list for the year. I am so excited about this author and I can't wait for the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12507214.Girl_of_Nightmares__Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__2_" title="Girl of Nightmares (Anna Dressed in Blood #2) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl of Nightmares</a>, to come out in 2012. Read it, read it, read it! I promise it will make you shudder, in the very best of ways.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2011/09/anna-dressed-in-blood-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a></i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9521177492367043121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_209750130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/209750130" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/209750130?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=leaves-awesomeness-behind">leaves-awesomeness-behind</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer209750130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12722593991451819830">I don't believe in ghosts. I don't believe in Ouji boards, aliens, loch ness monsters, abominable snowmen, poltergeists, republicans or any of that other stuff.<br/><br/>My little brother makes me watch those ghost hunter documentaries (I'm using that term lightly) and tries to show me the DARN FACTS, DAMNIT KATE! WHY CAN'T YOU SEE THAT THEY'RE REAL?<br/><br/>Funny how he believes in ghosts but not the continued statistical evidence that indicates women still suffer from inequality and, yes little brother, even in </span>
  <span id="freeText12722593991451819830" style="display:none">I don't believe in ghosts. I don't believe in Ouji boards, aliens, loch ness monsters, abominable snowmen, poltergeists, republicans or any of that other stuff.<br><br>My little brother makes me watch those ghost hunter documentaries (I'm using that term lightly) and tries to show me the DARN FACTS, DAMNIT KATE! WHY CAN'T YOU SEE THAT THEY'RE REAL?<br><br>Funny how he believes in ghosts but not the continued statistical evidence that indicates women still suffer from inequality and, yes little brother, even in western society. *Cue eye roll*<br><br>So keep that in mind when I say that this book scared the shit out of me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380359136ra/710301.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nothing is less fun then getting up in the middle of a dark night to tend to your son. You're creeping through the halls thinking over and over in your head, "Ghosts aren't real. Ghosts aren't real. Fuck what was that?! Nothing, okay? That was nothing because ghosts aren't real. Ghosts aren't real."<br><br>It's not a perfect novel. Apart from the pants-shitting terror, there is Cas to deal with. A lot of other reviews cover how his head space is occasionally annoying to be in. For me, that just felt like realism because if I were a badass, devil-may-care, teenage ghost hunter (if they existed, little bro) then I'd probably be really smarmy and annoying too.<br><br>What I really enjoyed was Anna and her relationship with Cas. Anna was like the girl next door. If the girl next door tore livers out of people to play hackey sack with, that is. She's this really lovely, murdersome, complicated ghost character. Although, I have to wonder how much she has to complain about really. I mean, sure, she's a dead horror-monster stuck in a house filled with the spiritual husks of her victims - but she died in a really awesome dress! And it even changes colour from white to red depending on how sadistically evil and murdery she feels at that time. Downside? I can't think of one.<br><br>I enjoyed the writing, the cast of characters, the plot and the pacing. I enjoyed pretty much everything about this novel.<br><br>I mean, who wouldn't want to spend the next two weeks pondering why the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interrobang" rel="nofollow noopener">interrobang</a> ever managed to fall out of popular use while roaming the dark halls of their house? <br><br>"What the hell was that?!"<br>"Is it going to eat me?!"<br>"Will they hear me scream!?"<br>"Why'd I read that stupid, fucking book... shitamIgoingtodie!?" <br><br><br><br><br>"When is the next one coming out?!" <br><br><br><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.blogspot.com/2012/01/anna-dressed-in-blook-by-kendare-blake.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335368i/694324.jpg" width="100" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_222963004" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222963004" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222963004?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like ghosts, I guess</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      Loads of GoodReads friends
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-didn-t-see-that-coming">i-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=quit-fucking-with-my-mind">quit-fucking-with-my-mind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable">it-wasn-t-all-that-but-enjoyable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222963004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13100764004045011252"><br/><b>Don't forget to check out the epic interview story with Kendare Blake over at <a href='http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/02/author-interview-with-kendare-blake-and-giveaway/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>!</b><br/><br/>Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br/><br/>Sometimes you read books that are visibly bad. So bad, in fact, that they make you want to throw yourself head first out a window, but you keep on reading and reading. You might even feel yourself losing your will to live about halfway through. But somehow, by the end of the book, you end up liking it anyway because it entertained you. The badness was just <i>that</i> entertaini</span>
  <span id="freeText13100764004045011252" style="display:none"><br><b>Don't forget to check out the epic interview story with Kendare Blake over at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/02/author-interview-with-kendare-blake-and-giveaway/" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>!</b><br><br>Actual rating: 2.5 stars<br><br>Sometimes you read books that are visibly bad. So bad, in fact, that they make you want to throw yourself head first out a window, but you keep on reading and reading. You might even feel yourself losing your will to live about halfway through. But somehow, by the end of the book, you end up liking it anyway because it entertained you. The badness was just <i>that</i> entertaining. Then, there are other books that are really good books, but just do nothing for you. <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> was the latter for me. There was nothing <i>wrong</i> with this book. It's just that ghost books and I don't get along. I typically stay away from only two paranormal creatures: ghosts and zombies. I probably would have never picked this book up on my own, but I figured I'd give <i>Anna Dressed in Blood</i> a shot for two reasons: 1) It came <i>highly</i> recommended to me from several reviewers and 2) The last time I read a zombie book (The Forest of Hands and Teeth) I really enjoyed it. So I was hoping to have a similar experience. Unfortunately, I didn't.<br><br><u>The three biggest issues I had with the book:</u><br><br><b>Cas</b><br><br>For the most part I did like him, but in the beginning I found him to be a bit conceited. When he first arrives in Thunder Bay, Ontario he walks around the school like he's way too cool to be there. To his credit, I guess he really is. I mean, he kills ghosts for a living. But the way those girls just fawned over him, like he was some Grecian god, was just a little over the top. <blockquote>
  <i>I make my way to her table, seeing eyes growing wider as I do. Ten or so other girls probably just developed instantaneous crushes on me, because they see that Carmel likes me.</i>
</blockquote> Then there was the issue with him being the only one able to kill ghosts. He kept repeating, "I'm the only one who can do this" and I kept asking, "Oh, yeah? Why? Why, Cas? What makes you so <i>speshul</i>?" Yes, I realize he comes from a long line of ghost <s>busters</s> hunters, but why his family? What makes his bloodline different from anyone else? I needed background info and I never got it. <br><br><b>Anna</b><br><br>Anna Dressed in Blood. I was told to read this book with the lights on. Usually, I scare very easily. I wasn't scared one bit while reading. At first, when Cas "runs into" Anna, I was thinking, "Uh, oh. It's about to go <b>down</b>." And for a minute it did. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Anna tore <s>dipshit</s> Mike in half. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was shocked and even more shocked that I liked it. I was starting to think that everyone who recommended me this book was on to something. Anna. Oh, Anna. Why couldn't you remain scary? <br><br>This is what I wanted from you:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361202i/712090._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I wanted you to run around angry, strike some fear in people's hearts, make me afraid of the dark for a few nights, <i>tear some shit up.</i><br><br>But this is what I got instead:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361202i/712091.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For some odd reason you didn't have the urge to hurt Cas, which is never explained. Again, why is this kid so <i>speshul</i>? <br><br><b>The Romance</b><br><br>This is honestly where the book started to lose me. Killer vindictive girl running around killing people? I can handle that. Cas going all "goo-goo eyes" over a dead girl? Yeah, um...it didn't work for me. But who am I to judge? If Cas likes it when Anna makes her eyes go black, her veins crawl up her arms, her deep, neck wound opening up to create her flowing blood dress, calling her <i>"My Anna"</i>, then that is totally his business. I just didn't see where that relationship was supposed to be headed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Then they made out on the front porch of her possessed house and all I could think was, "Ew<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www">www</a>..." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It was different, I'll give Blake that, but it just didn't work for me.<br><br><u>Other things that bothered me:</u><br><br>I did not understand the mythology behind Cas' knife and the villain. It went straight over my head. I felt maybe that part could have been explained better. However, I suppose it's entirely possible that my little, simple brain could not grasp the complex explanation given. Maybe.<br><br>Cas' mother being so accepting of her son's profession. If your husband is killed while ghost hunting, wouldn't you try everything you could to have him not go down the same road? <br><br>Thomas' grandfather says he wanted Cas originally to kill Anna because she was acting different. I thought that was going to be significant to the plot, but we never found out why her behavior had initially changed.<br><br>I took issue how the kids in the story had so little empathy for their friends who were killed. When <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mike <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> dies, Will makes up a some half-assed story about him walking home alone (bold is mine):<blockquote>
  <i>“We tell the cops that we drove around for a while. Then...got mad about Carmel and Cas and got out of the truck. None of us could stop him. <b>He said he was going to walk home, and since it wasn’t that far away, we didn’t think anything of it.</b> When he didn’t show at school today, we figured that he was hung over.” </i>
</blockquote> But then when the police question Cas and Carmel a few days later (I've taken his name out due to spoilers)...<blockquote>
  <i>“<b>You are aware that...lived at least ten miles from the area you’re talking about</b>,” Officer Roebuck said.<br>“No, I didn’t know,” I reply.<br>“We tried to stop him,” Carmel pipes up.</i>
</blockquote> Now, I'm not sure if that inconsistency was on purpose, but Will is supposed to be this guy's best friend. He wouldn't notice that the story he made up was off? Most of the time in the book it felt like the kids were too busy about getting blamed for a crime that they never took time to <i>care</i> that someone was murdered. <br><br>Last but not least: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tybalt being eaten by the "boogeyman" type ghost. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That part really made me angry.<br><br><u>Things I liked:</u><br><br><b>1.</b> I thought Carmel and Cas were going to end up together. I was happy to see Blake didn't go for that very easy trope. <br><br><b>2.</b> Anna's story was very sad and made it easy to be sympathetic towards her. <br><br><b>3.</b> Never saw the villain coming. He was confusing, but unpredictable.<br><br>All in all, I would still recommend this book to other people because the biggest reason why I didn't love it was because I just don't like ghosts. *shrug*<br><br>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13100764004045011252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText12266579974592572968" style="display:none">This book started all for me. This is the turning moment when I started to read the majority of my books in English. I was in Berlin for a couple of weeks and finished all my books. So, I went into a bookstore. And there it was in the English section, right next to the Fifty Shades of Grey (don't ask me about the logic behind that). <br />I was so scared because I never read a "normal" book in English but wow. I ended up loving the book so much. <br />I remember reading it the whole train ride from Berlin to Prague, I was totally immersed by the story. <br />I just enjoyed everything about it. I loved Cas. I adored Anna in her demonical moments. The basement scene was the best in the whole book.<br />And the ending? I need more of that!</span>

<div id="review_620034913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/620034913" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/620034913?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=creepfest">creepfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer620034913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6826215897913769455"><b>I'M ABOUT TO SPAM THE SHIT OUT OF YOU WITH SUPERNATURAL SHENANNIGANS. SO IF GIF-HAPPY REVIEWS AREN'T YOUR THING, LOOK AWAY NOW.</b><br/><br/>I picked this up for one reason and one reason alone.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427385438i/14267448._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This past week, I had the plague - given to me by a yet unidentified coworker. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <br/>
  <b>YOU BETTER HOPE I NEVER FIND YOU, MOTHER FUCKER.<b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427583020i/14289508.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/></b></b>
 <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> During my many days off, I decided to distract myself from the threat of exorcist-style spray painting my bedroom by binge-watching Supernatural. <br/><br/>Best. De</span>
  <span id="freeText6826215897913769455" style="display:none"><b>I'M ABOUT TO SPAM THE SHIT OUT OF YOU WITH SUPERNATURAL SHENANNIGANS. SO IF GIF-HAPPY REVIEWS AREN'T YOUR THING, LOOK AWAY NOW.</b><br><br>I picked this up for one reason and one reason alone.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427385438i/14267448._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This past week, I had the plague - given to me by a yet unidentified coworker. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <b>YOU BETTER HOPE I NEVER FIND YOU, MOTHER FUCKER.<b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427583020i/14289508.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></b></b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> During my many days off, I decided to distract myself from the threat of exorcist-style spray painting my bedroom by binge-watching Supernatural. <br><br>Best. Decision. Ever. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391570268ra/8412628.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>SO DO I, DEAN. SO DO I.</b><br><br>And that's exactly what I was hoping to find in this book. It didn't disappoint. Let me set the scene for you: A dark road. A classic car. A young badass with an "I don't give a shit" attitude who hunts ghosts. Oh, and his name is Cas, his father is dead, and he's hell bent on avenging him. <br><br>Hmmmm…this all seems very familiar. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/527501.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So be warned, Supernatural fanatics, some of this strikes quite close to home. At least in the beginning. I still recommend giving it a try, because once the story gets rolling, the plot truly stands on its own. <br><br>And if you're worried that it might be too scary for you, think again. I'm a wuss, and I only got creeped out twice. Blake's haunting prose makes this much more atmospheric than frightening. <br><br><i>"We're driving close to the lake now, and I can hear Superior whisper to me in waves about all of the dead things she hides beneath her surface, staring through the depths with murky eyes and fish-bitten cheeks."</i><br><br>The one thing that keeps this from being a five star read for me are the tropes. Insta-love chief among them. Look, I get it, teenagers are blinded by hormones, blah, blah, blah. But how the ever-loving fuck can you fall in love with a psychotic, rampaging murder-ghost? And you're telling me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that after kissing a dead girl you start to think about your future with her? AS IF YOU HAVE ONE? You're going to keep aging and she'll be sixteen forever, dude.<br><br>*cue Dazed and Confused Matthew McConaughey flashback*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397621125ra/9302386.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Too bad. I'm not spelling it out for you. Go watch the movie because it's fucking awesome. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Okay, so tropes aside, this was a solid read. I quickly found myself invested in Cas's story, the pacing had an organic momentum that never felt forced, I didn't see the plot twists coming, and as soon as I set it down I wanted to pick up the next. Which I'm about to do. So if you'll excuse me, I'll leave you with this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427583020ra/14289509.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6826215897913769455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_212657144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212657144" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/212657144?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212657144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2670745477166591751">Oh <b>Anna</b>…you strong, <b>saucy</b>, serial-killing, <b>ripping-bodies-in-two</b> “ghostess with the mostess”…where have you been all my life? <br/><br/>This book is a few <b>menu items</b> to the right of my normal literary <b>diet</b> and so I want extend a warm thank you to my <b>YA sommeliers</b>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4622890-emily-may' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emily May</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wendy Darling</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4551536-maja' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maja</a>, for turning me on to this. You took right and proper care of me with this recommendation, and while I couldn’t quite bring myself to give away the 4th star, I did find mucho to enjoy about this novel plan to gr</span>
  <span id="freeText2670745477166591751" style="display:none">Oh <b>Anna</b>…you strong, <b>saucy</b>, serial-killing, <b>ripping-bodies-in-two</b> “ghostess with the mostess”…where have you been all my life? <br><br>This book is a few <b>menu items</b> to the right of my normal literary <b>diet</b> and so I want extend a warm thank you to my <b>YA sommeliers</b>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4622890-emily-may" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily May</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling" rel="nofollow noopener">Wendy Darling</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4551536-maja" rel="nofollow noopener">Maja</a>, for turning me on to this. You took right and proper care of me with this recommendation, and while I couldn’t quite bring myself to give away the 4th star, I did find mucho to enjoy about this novel plan to grab the sequel when it comes out (after it's been properly vetted and cleared by the <b>YA Triumvirate</b>). <br><br><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br><br>With all of the wonderful reviews already committed to GR for this novel, I'll keep this portion fairly sweet. Meet young <s>Dean Winchester</s> Cas Lowood:<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Classic%20TV/?action=view&amp;current=SupernaturalSeason6-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359578i/710526.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Cas travels around the country with his Wiccan Mother killing (so to speak) ghosts.<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Hollywood%20moviess/?action=view&amp;current=ghost_patrick_swayze-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380359578i/710527.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>…Dammit, where were you when we needed you.</i> <br><br>Cas comes from a long line of ghost exterminators and took over from his father when daddy got murdered by a particularly nasty apparition. Now, armed with his family’s special ghost-killing knife called an <b>athame</b>, Cas and his mom have arrived in Thunder Bay, Ontario to dispose of a particularly nasty ghost known as Anna Dressed in Blood. It seems Anna has been butchering, and I mean slicing, dicing, mincing and tearing to chunky shreds of human jerky, anyone stupid enough to venture inside the house in which she resides. <br><br><b><u>THOUGHTS</u>:</b><br><br><b>Things I loved:</b><br><br>** <u>The Mythology</u>: I thought the author did a stellar job of developing a mythology that was familiar and instantly comfortable for the reader and yet was also accented with enough unique frills and imaginative flavor to make the fantasy/horror elements feel daisy fresh and original. I also thought there was a depth to the world that the author did a great job of creating without resorting to a lot of info dumpiness. The author kept the focus on telling the story and deftly spiced in info goodies from time to time as a happy seasoning. <br><br>** <u>The Daddy Factor</u>: As a dad, one metric I use to judge a story like this is to ask myself the following the two questions: <br><br>(1) Are the leading female characters people that I would want my girls to either befriend, emulate and/or identify with? <br><br>(2) Are the main male characters guys that I would want my daughters to associate with or fall for… <i>(eventually I mean…when they are in their 30s and have completed Med School, traveled the world and written their first best seller)?</i> <br><br>For both (1) and (2), with a few minor pickies, this book gets gold stars and a resounding YES from me. I thought each of Anna (supernatural beastliness aside), Carmel and Cas’ mother were richly drawn characters that I really came to appreciate over the course of the story. Despite some minor <b>Cas-bashing</b> below, I thought he was a good guy and his “talented” friend Thomas was terrific. <br><br>Of course, there were the usual suspects of stereotypical ass jacking jocks that I thought was a smidgen too easy and a few of the supporting females were a tinkle too <b>googly-eyed</b> over Cas for my gag reflex…but again, that’s dad talking. Overall, Ms. Blake gets an “A” on characters. <br><br>** <u>Anna</u>: Anna gets her own special mention because I thought she was <b>slathered</b> in <b>special sauce</b> and I was smitten from the moment she ripped that shit sack in two. However, what truly raised the bar for me from cool character to mega memorable was Anna’s heart-wrenching story and the origin of her current predicament. All that strength and power and yet saddled by loss, longing and an almost unimaginable load of grief. She tugged on my heart strings like a lawn mower chain. <br><br>**<u>The Villain</u>: I don’t want to say more and spoil the fun but…nicely done.<br><br>**<u>The Opening Scene</u>: What a superb beginning to the book. The intro to Cas and his first job that we tag along for is outstanding. Grabbed me right away. <br><br>**<u>Anna and Cas</u>: The romance/friendship was perfectly done. No over the top melodrama or swoon-filled heart-palpitations, but a strong, believable bond based on mutual respect and soul-mateness. <br><br>**<u>Cas</u>: I’m going to end with Cas as he has the distinctly dubious honor of being on both my <b>pro</b> and my <b>faux</b> list. Overall, I really like Cas and I think he was a positive aspect of the book. At both the beginning and the end, I thought he performed admirably.<br><br>However…<br> <br><b>Things that irked me:</b><br><br>**<u>Cas as James Dean Winchester</u>: The Cas as the dark, brooding loner who knows he’s just a little too cool and grown up for the rest of his piers…nails on a chalkboard to me. A few teeth-gritting examples: <br><br><i> “Still, people’s eyes tend to linger on me longer, because even though I’m new, I don’t move like it.”</i><br><br><i>“Or Maybe I’m just damn easy on the eyes.”</i><br><br><i> “Queen bees are just part of the job. Sometimes that’s hard to remember.”</i><br><br><i> “I’m too proud to turn around – I’ve been through too much scary shit to be put off by any human attacker.”</i><br><br>In a word…BARF!! I really struggled with this <b>I'm so battitude</b> and the whole causeless rebel posturing. Still, to his credit, nothing Cas actually <u>did</u> ever rated him anywhere on the asshole scale and he turned out, as I mentioned above, to be a great guy and an excellent character. Thus, I'm going to chalk the above up to Ms. Blake having a difficult time finding her “guy” voice. <br><br>**<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<u> Tybalt</u>: The swinging of the tail by Mr. Nasty bugged the shit out of me. I am a major animal lover and cats are my numero uno. I loved the character of Tybalt and how he could sense ghosts and I just thought that him getting the snack treatment was…just…plain…wrong!! There were plenty of people to chew on.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Overall, the positives significantly outweighed the relatively minor gripes and I thought this was a terrific story. I am not the typical target audience for this and so my thorough enjoyment of this is high praise indeed. The writing was good and the story-telling was excellent with nice pacing, interesting info nuggets and some well placed chills. <br><br>3.5 Stars. Recommended! <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2670745477166591751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1223799987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223799987" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223799987?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223799987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11624326223940280617">Dear <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake' title='Kendare Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kendare Blake</a>,<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456157547ra/18197879.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Sincerely,<br/><br/>A girl who never sleeps with the lights off.<br/><br/>Before I jump into raving about this <b>deliciously creepy</b> book, I have to give you some backround details. <b>I don't do horror.</b> The only exception to my stay-away-from-things-that-will-disturb-your-beauty-sleep rule is the summer I spent binge-watching Supernatural, and let's just say that my motivations to start this series were far from noble.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455480646ra/18107884.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yes, I am that shallow. But the thing is, after the first few nights I couldn't lo</span>
  <span id="freeText11624326223940280617" style="display:none">Dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake" title="Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Kendare Blake</a>,<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456157547ra/18197879.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Sincerely,<br><br>A girl who never sleeps with the lights off.<br><br>Before I jump into raving about this <b>deliciously creepy</b> book, I have to give you some backround details. <b>I don't do horror.</b> The only exception to my stay-away-from-things-that-will-disturb-your-beauty-sleep rule is the summer I spent binge-watching Supernatural, and let's just say that my motivations to start this series were far from noble.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455480646ra/18107884.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, I am that shallow. But the thing is, after the first few nights I couldn't look at the ceiling without imagining a dead woman hanging and bursting into flames, I became seriously addicted to the story of the gorgeous and badass ghost/vampire/demon-hunting brothers. And <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Dressed in Blood</a> took me back to those wonderful, spooky days.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Move, hunt, kill. Like lather, rinse, and repeat.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Theseus Cassio 'Cas' Lowood is a <b>ghost hunter</b>, just like his father before him, and his grandfather before him. Each kill, each time he sends a restless dead to the other side, is one step closer to his secret mission; to face the ghost that brutally murdered his father. When he gets a tip about a gloomy Canadian city inhabited by a dead girl that mutilates her victims, he knows he has to investigate her. Anna. Anna Dressed in Blood, a girl who died under mysterious circumstances that turned her into a ghost somehow different. More aware. More ruthless. More savage. After getting beaten and witnessing a classmate torn from limb to limb, he knows he can't simply kill her with his mystical blade. And so he dwelves into her secrets and the story of her death, only to find out that the Evil he's up against is more terrifying that he could possibly imagine. And that the dead girl is the only one to make him feel alive.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Anna, my strong, terrifying Anna.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Dressed in Blood</a> is a <b>bone-chilling paranormal story</b> laced with <b>tragedies</b> and <b>gruesome murders</b>. It holds your interest from the first page to the last, and frantically claws its way to your heart until it smothers it in a bleeding embrace. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake" title="Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Kendare Blake</a> makes you face some vivid images you can't get out of your head, and leaves you pondering on the unfairness of it all, and the horrible realization that <b>the living are worse than the dead</b>. Behind every spirit on a killing spree and massacres that twist your insides, there is a living and breathing human, who, driven by his passions, inflicted pain and triggered the series of unnecessary murders. Because it is common knowledge that the ones who don't cross the other side are those who met a violent ending, those with unfinished business. And I commend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake" title="Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Kendare Blake</a> for highlighting this terrible truth amidst the blood and gore. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But hey, at least we’ll have this strange story to tell, love and death and blood and daddy-issues. And holy crap, I’m a psychiatrist’s wet dream.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There was something <b>bitter</b> and <b>sarcastic</b> in the narration of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Dressed in Blood</a>. Cas is a superbly depicted character, whose fear and frustration and longing become your own. He doesn't elaborate much on details, but he paints the city of Thunder Bay clearly, and you can't help but smell the rosemary and the herbs in his wiccan mother's kitchen, feel Tybalt the cat rubbing his head on your feet, hear the leaves rustling and step into Anna's haunted house, only to gag on the decay and despair. Cas doesn't spare us the awful sight of the victims he encounters. But he also doesn't stay there more than necessary. The story of him finding Anna, and friends, and a place he doesn't wish to leave for the first time, is his story of becoming an adult. Of coming across new and frightening feelings, of finally facing the demons of his past, accepting help when he needs it and giving help, even if it is to a dead girl trapped in her violent nature. Anna is a tragic figure. A victim and a killer. Horrible and fascinating. Beneath her murderous rampage hides a girl who didn't have a chance to live her life the way she wanted it. You cry at the unfairness. Your stomach churns and your hands turn clammy before the horror. Your heart threatens to burst from your chest. Yet you wouldn't trade this <b>ghastly and eerie atmosphere</b> with anything in the world.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You make me want things I can't have.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Dressed in Blood</a> was a stunning read, and if you're into paranormal and forbidden love stories soaked in blood and coated in smoke, you'll definitely love it!<br><br><i>Visit <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a> for <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/8-kat-reviews/723-annadressedinblood" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11624326223940280617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_198419000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198419000" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198419000?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198419000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6886067923857132973"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_' title='Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna Dressed in Blood</a> was a surprisingly good read. I'm not exactly sure what I was expecting, something typical of young adult urban fantasy perhaps... same old characters, lots of romancing, maybe even an interesting little mystery to give the book some semblance of plot if we're lucky. I was really quite pleased with this exciting, slightly spooky, and wholly entertaining start to the series. <br/><br/>I cannot stress highly enough how glad I am that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake' title='Kendare Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kendare Blake</a> wrote a romance that was gradually</span>
  <span id="freeText6886067923857132973" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Dressed in Blood</a> was a surprisingly good read. I'm not exactly sure what I was expecting, something typical of young adult urban fantasy perhaps... same old characters, lots of romancing, maybe even an interesting little mystery to give the book some semblance of plot if we're lucky. I was really quite pleased with this exciting, slightly spooky, and wholly entertaining start to the series. <br><br>I cannot stress highly enough how glad I am that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4086715.Kendare_Blake" title="Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Kendare Blake</a> wrote a romance that was gradually introduced as the story moved along and the characters developed. It would have been so easy - and not at all unexpected - for the author to just create an insta-loving, destiny bound pair, completely devoid of all chemistry and certain to be walking off into the sunset holding hands and singing folk songs at the novel's close. But no. I was able to see how the relationship changed and developed and it was not unclear to me why these two would fall for one another.<br><br>Also, I had been unaware that the protagonist was male, just assuming that the book would be told from Anna's point of view. I will say of Cas what I said of another Cas(tiel) who I enjoyed reading about: he was easy to relate to, but at the same time he was believably male. Something which appears to be rather difficult if books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11455096.Tempest__Tempest___1_" title="Tempest (Tempest, #1) by Julie Cross" rel="nofollow noopener">Tempest</a> are anything to go by. In this case, Cas is a ghost hunter just like his father was before him and he travels around the world attempting to rid it of spirits that are left with enough supernatural energy to be able to physically harm humans. Someday he hopes to avenge his father's death at the hands of a particularly vicious ghost. But before that, he has one final test. A spook to rival all spooks, a powerful and wicked goddess of death... Anna Korlov. Anna dressed in blood.<br><br>The story had me interested from the very first chapter and kept me glued to the pages throughout. The book actually has two big mysteries to solve and an interesting twist towards the end so I remained thoroughly mystified. Some people found this book scary, others not so much, I would say that there's one part which you wouldn't want to read when you're alone in your house at night but other than that it's more gory and gross than actually frightening. So beware if you're squeamish but expect a wild and exciting ride.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6886067923857132973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_228853301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228853301" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228853301?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11663424-anna-dressed-in-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228853301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14792666881703927572">First off, I feel I should discuss the cover art: I know, I know--everyone loves this cover. Unfortunately it doesn't do anything for me. Look, I stopped being <s>fooled</s> wowed by cover art after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_' title='Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen</a>. That's a lie--the cover for the third Paranormalcy book makes me ridiculously happy, but at least I'm fairly certain I'll like that book since I like the first two books in the series. <br/><br/>In my opinion the following would have made a better cover for Anna Dressed In Blood:<br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362114i/713233.jpg' alt='Carrie,Prom Queen,Anna Dressed in Blood,They're All Gonna Laugh' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>Infinitely better,</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14792666881703927572" style="display:none">First off, I feel I should discuss the cover art: I know, I know--everyone loves this cover. Unfortunately it doesn't do anything for me. Look, I stopped being <s>fooled</s> wowed by cover art after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_" title="Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen</a>. That's a lie--the cover for the third Paranormalcy book makes me ridiculously happy, but at least I'm fairly certain I'll like that book since I like the first two books in the series. <br><br>In my opinion the following would have made a better cover for Anna Dressed In Blood:<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362114i/713233.jpg" alt="Carrie,Prom Queen,Anna Dressed in Blood,They're All Gonna Laugh" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Infinitely better, don't you think? I mean, at least she's <i>actually</i> dressed in blood.</i><br><br>Moving on...<br><br>You know how Cake Pops are the newest, coolest thing in baked goods? And everyone's all "O mai, it'ss teh caaaaaaaake popssssssss!"? And you're standing there thinking, <i>sure they're cute but they're just little glorified cupcakes on sticks</i>? Well, let me start by saying: Anna Dressed in Blood is the Cake Pop of the publishing industry. Sure it's cute(-ish) but I fail to see what the big deal is. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362114i/713234.jpg" alt="Ghostly Cake Pops" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Seriously, what's the big deal?</i><br><br>I've read several reviews that claim this book is hilarious and disgusting and terrifying. <i>Plus!</i> <i>Awesome Characters!</i> <i>Weird Romance!</i> I was under the impression Anna Dressed in Blood was the YA version of Fargo, except with a Very Murdery Ghost instead of a woodchipper. And I was all, <i>sign me up!</i> <br><br>My mistake was falling for the hype &amp; actually believing the rumors. <br><br><br><b>It's not laugh-out-loud funny</b> <br><br><blockquote> <i>"Hey" he says, pulling up a chair. "Aren't you going to eat your Jell-o?"<br>"I effing hate green Jell-o," I reply, and push it his way.<br>"I hate it too. I was just asking."<br>I laugh. "Don't make me hurt my ribs, you dick."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Bahahahahaha. So funny, right? <br><br>Kidding! I'm not sure which parts were supposed to be funny, actually. Even during the 30% of this book I did enjoy I never laughed, not even in my head. I'd have settled for a "that's what she said" joke. I'm not too picky when it comes to humor. <br><br><br><b>It's not terrifying. (Not even a little.)</b> <br><br>I keep reading reviews that claim this book is scary. It isn't. Yeah, there's a ghost (a couple, actually). Yeah, Anna likes to make it look like her dress is dripping with blood. Yeah, she murders people. But it just so happens that none of that scared me. If there was a demonic clown in this book then I might have been a little frightened. But, alas, no demonic clowns. <br><br><br> <b>It's not a paranormal romance</b><br><br>As far as I'm concerned it's not PNR unless the romance is a major part of the story. Believe me when I say this: the romance is hardly even present. What little romance there is between Cas and Anna is forced and awkward. I only knew they were in love because I was told as much. There was no flirting. No longing glances. No blushing and looking away. No showing off. Now I can't even remember if there is any kissing. I think there might be a kissing scene, but the romance is so minor I just don't remember. The only things Cas and Anna had in common is both their fathers are dead and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ their mothers are witches <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Other than that, I can't think of anything else they might have in common. I would have loved to hear that they both liked the same subjects in school, read the same books, or even that they shared a deep passion for pie, but that never happened. Their conversations consisted of Cas questioning Anna about who killed her, the people she killed and how she feels about it, ghost killing, nightmares, and how to stop the gruesome murders happening in Thunder Bay. <br><br>I don't know, maybe that's what passes for romance in Canada these days. <br><br>The other romance is more interesting, in that it's an unconventional human pairing. I loves me an unconventional love story. That said, it's still another romance that's only present because we're told as much. Sure, Thomas the Nerd is crushing hard-core on Carmel, the hottest girl in school, but I fail to see why she might return his feelings. He's described as looking like a 12-year-old with unkempt orangey-red hair. He dresses ugly, he's awkward and he has a bit of a chip on his shoulder (which, by the way, conveniently disappears early on in the story). Yes, Thomas is nice to Carmel and worships the ground she walks on, but that's pretty much how everyone treats her. She's the hot girl, remember? So...what's in it for Carmel? I want to know that she finds him attractive on an intellectual level, or that it's his sense of humor and confidence that she finds irresistibly sexy (by the way, he's not funny <i>but he needs to be</i> because he is the plucky side-kick), or that she loves him because he really wants to be with her for her personality and not just her looks. <br><br><br><b>It's not disgusting</b><br><br>I'm not going to lie to you. All the gory details are vague at best. So if you're not into that sort of thing, don't worry, you're pretty safe. That said, I feel I should warn you: yes, there is some dismemberment, and, yes, it is a little abrupt when it happens the first time, but other than that... *shrug* I've actually seen worse (on tv). <br><br> <a href="http://photobucket.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362114ra/713235.gif" alt="The Walking Dead gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>That. Just. Happened. Now please excuse me as I dry-heave for the next 30 seconds.</i><br><br>Which brings me to my next point: <br><br><br><b>I need the characters to show some genuine emotion</b><br><br>Look, I know I just said that I've seen worse and that's why the gory descriptions didn't affect me. It's just that, had I seen someone dismembered <i>IN REAL LIFE</i>, I'd: 1) vomit 2) vomit some more 3) run away screaming 4) cry 5) dry-heave just thinking about it 6) have nightmares for the rest of my life 7) work it out in therapy. <br><br>And that's what I'd do if I never even knew the person. <br><br>These kids? Have never seen any real (read: not hallucinations) dismembered bodies, ever. So when they see it happen to people they actually know, I want them to do at least one of the following: 1) run away screaming 2) go into hysterics while standing there 3) go into shock 4) huddle in a corner 5) vomit 6) dry-heave 7) cry about it for more then a paragraph 8) have nightmares 9) call the cops 10) feel survivor guilt.<br><br>None of that happened, which is why these teens seem so robotic. <br><br>Also? I have a problem with the amount of time these kids spent on getting their stories straight. They spent more time working on alibis then they did thinking about the kids that died horrible, painful deaths. It's seriously disturbing how little they spent thinking about the dead kids or the dead kids' families. And don't tell me it doesn't really matter how they felt about the dead kids because they were bullies who deserved to die.<br><br>It's called empathy. Look it up. <br><br><br><br><br><br>(I have so much more to say but I don't know if I'll be able to finish this review before next week. I'm posting it now as a sort of early Thanksgiving present for everyone. You're welcome. <br><br>Happy Thanksgiving!)<br><br><br><br><br>----<br><br>You can bet I have a lot to say about this book. I'll start working on a full review soon. Until then I feel I should mention that I am in the minority with this one. If you're thinking about reading this, go ahead and do so. Chances are you'll probably like it. <br><br>If you also don't like this book leave a comment below so we can trash this book together. 1.5 stars. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14792666881703927572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204875078?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
